<p>As is typical of pistols chambered in .40 S&amp;W, each of the standard Glock models (22, 23, and 27) may be easily converted to the corresponding <a href="/wiki/.357_SIG" title=".357 SIG">.357 SIG</a> chambering (Glock 31, 32, and 33, respectively) simply by replacing the barrel. No other parts need to be replaced, as the .40 S&amp;W magazines will feed the .357 SIG rounds.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id=".380_ACP">.380 ACP</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glock&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: .380 ACP">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The first two <a href="/wiki/.380_ACP" title=".380 ACP">.380 ACP</a> models are primarily intended for markets which prohibit civilian ownership of firearms chambered in military calibers such as 9×19mm Parabellum.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>Due to the relatively low <a href="/wiki/Bolt_thrust" title="Bolt thrust">bolt thrust</a> of the .380 ACP cartridge, the locked-breech design of the Glock 19 and Glock 26 was minimally modified for the Glock 25 and Glock 28 to implement unlocked breech operation. It operates via <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blowback_(arms)" title="Blowback (arms)">straight blowback</a> of the slide. This required modification of the locking surfaces on the barrel, as well as a redesign of the former locking block. Unusual for a blowback design, the barrel is not fixed to the frame. It moves rearward in recoil until it is tilted below the slide, similar to the standard locked-breech system. The reduced size and mass of the Glock 42 required return to the Glock-standard locked-breech design.</p>
<ul>
<li>The <b>Glock 25</b><span id="Glock_25"></span>, introduced in 1995, is a blowback derivative of the compact (102 mm (4.0 in) barrel) Glock 19. The magazine capacity is 15 rounds. Standard fixed sight elevation is 6.9 mm, unlike the 6.5 mm elevation used for the 9×19mm models.</li>
<li>The <b>Glock 28</b><span id="Glock_28"></span>, introduced in 1997, is a blowback derivative of the subcompact (87 mm (3.4 in) barrel) Glock 26. The standard magazine capacity is 10 rounds, but the 15-round Glock 25 magazine will function in the Glock 28. Standard fixed-sight elevation is 6.9 mm, unlike the 6.5 mm elevation used for the 9×19mm Parabellum models.</li>
<li>The <b>Glock 42</b><span id="Glock_42"></span>, introduced in 2014, is an all-new locked-breech "slimline" (83 mm (3.3 in) barrel) design. The single-stack magazine is unique to this model, with a capacity of six rounds. It is Glock's smallest model ever made and is manufactured in the USA, which unlike the Glock 25 and 28, allows domestic sales in that market.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id=".357_SIG">.357 SIG</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glock&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: .357 SIG">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Glock33_big.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="603" data-file-width="924" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Glock33_big.jpg/220px-Glock33_big.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Glock33_big.jpg/330px-Glock33_big.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Glock33_big.jpg/440px-Glock33_big.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Glock33_big.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The subcompact Glock 33 in .357 SIG</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li>The <b>Glock 31</b><span id="Glock_31"></span> is a <a href="/wiki/.357_SIG" title=".357 SIG">.357 SIG</a> variant of the full-sized Glock 22. The standard magazine capacity of the Glock 31 is 15 rounds.</li>
<li>The <b>Glock 32</b><span id="Glock_32"></span> is a .357 SIG variant of the compact Glock 23. The standard magazine capacity of the Glock 32 is 13 rounds.</li>
<li>The <b>Glock 33</b><span id="Glock_33"></span> is a .357 SIG variant of the subcompact Glock 27. The standard magazine capacity of the Glock 33 is 9 rounds.</li>
</ul>
<p>As is typical of pistols chambered in .357 SIG, each of the standard Glock models (31, 32, and 33) may be easily converted to the corresponding .40 S&amp;W chambering (Glock 22, 23, and 27, respectively) simply by replacing the barrel. No other parts need to be replaced, as the .357 SIG magazines will feed the .40 S&amp;W round.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id=".45_GAP">.45 GAP</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glock&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: .45 GAP">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Glock pistols chambered for the <a href="/wiki/.45_GAP" title=".45 GAP">.45 GAP</a> (and the .45 ACP) feature <a href="/wiki/Octagon" title="Octagon">octagonal</a> <a href="/wiki/Polygonal_rifling" title="Polygonal rifling">polygonal rifling</a> rather than the hexagonal shaped bores used for models in most other chamberings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Glock_FAQ_63-1"><a href="#cite_note-Glock_FAQ-63">[63]</a></sup> Octagonal rifling provides a better gas seal in relatively large diameter rifled bores, since an octagon resembles a <a href="/wiki/Circle" title="Circle">circle</a> more closely than a hexagon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barrel_History_47-2"><a href="#cite_note-Barrel_History-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>The <b>Glock 37</b><span id="Glock_37"></span> is a .45 GAP version of the Glock 17. It uses a wider, beveled slide, larger barrel, and different magazine, but is otherwise similar to the Glock 17. The Glock 37 first appeared in 2003. It was designed to offer ballistic performance comparable with the .45 ACP in the frame size of the Glock 17. The concern with the size of the Glock 20/21 has been addressed by the Glock 36, 21SF, and 30SF, all of which featured reduced-size frames. The standard magazine capacity of the Glock 37 is 10 rounds.</li>
<li>The <b>Glock 38</b><span id="Glock_38"></span> is a .45 GAP version of the compact Glock 19.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> The standard magazine capacity of the Glock 38 is 8 rounds.</li>
<li>The <b>Glock 39</b><span id="Glock_39"></span> is a .45 GAP version of the subcompact Glock 26. The standard magazine capacity of the Glock 39 is 6 rounds.</li>
</ul>

<td colspan="11" style="text-align: left"><b>Notes:</b>
<ul>
<li>Glock pistols marked by "*" indicate that a "Gen4" model is available. The Glock 40 and Glock 41 are only made in the "Gen4" frame.</li>
<li>Glock pistols marked by "^" indicate that an "MOS" (Modular Optic System) model is available. The Glock 40 is only made in the "MOS" configuration.</li>
<li>Glock pistols designated by "C" after the model number are equipped with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ported_barrel" title="Ported barrel">ported barrels</a> and slides to compensate for muzzle rise.</li>
<li>Glock 18/18C pistols are 9×19mm Parabellum <a href="/wiki/Selective_fire" title="Selective fire">select-fire</a> <a href="/wiki/Machine_pistol" title="Machine pistol">machine pistols</a> and not available to the general public in most countries.</li>
<li>Glock pistols designated "SF" are "short-framed". They have 2.5 mm (0.098 in) shorter trigger reach from the back of the grip and the heel of the pistol is shortened by 4 mm (0.16 in) for the full-sized framed Glock 20 and 21. The reduction in the heel of the Glock 29 and 30 is not as pronounced.</li>
<li>Glock 25 or 28 pistols are not available to the general public in the United States, because a small pistol chambered for the .380 ACP cartridge does not meet the "sporting purposes" criteria for importation of pistols under the <a href="/wiki/Gun_Control_Act_of_1968" title="Gun Control Act of 1968">Gun Control Act of 1968</a>, according to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BATFE" title="BATFE">BATFE</a>'s point system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> The Glock 42, however, is not subject to those regulations because it is produced in the United States rather than imported, allowing it to be sold on the civilian market.</li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Regional_variants">Regional variants</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glock&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Regional variants">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Glock25SDN.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1152" data-file-width="1536" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Glock25SDN.jpg/220px-Glock25SDN.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Glock25SDN.jpg/330px-Glock25SDN.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Glock25SDN.jpg/440px-Glock25SDN.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Glock25SDN.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Mexico forces Glock model 25 SDN pistol.</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li>The Glock Mariner and Glock Tactical are versions of various Glock pistols sold in the Philippines with an adjustable rear sight, extended slide stop, maritime spring cups, and an engraved slide with the words 'MARINER' or 'TACTICAL'.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-International_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-International-74">[74]</a></sup></li>
<li>The Glock 17A is a variant produced with a 120 mm (4.7 in) extended barrel that protrudes from the slide visibly. It is intended for the <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australian</a> market to conform to local laws regarding barrel length created after the <a href="/wiki/Monash_University_shooting" title="Monash University shooting">Monash University shooting</a> and are supplied with 10-round magazines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></li>
<li>The Glock 17S is a variant with an external, frame-mounted, manual <a href="/wiki/Safety_(firearms)" title="Safety (firearms)">safety</a>. Small numbers of this variant were made for the <a href="/wiki/Tasmania" title="Tasmania">Tasmanian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israeli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistani</a>, and perhaps several South American security forces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> They are stamped "17", not "17S". They resemble, but are distinguishable from, standard Glock 17 pistols that have been fitted with the after-market Cominolli safety.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> An additional safety variant Glock 17 that was tested by the British Military included a frame safety similar to that found on the British service rifle, the SA-80.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></li>
<li>The Glock 17Pro version is produced exclusively for the <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finnish</a> market.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-International_74-1"><a href="#cite_note-International-74">[74]</a></sup> It has these alterations from the standard Glock 17: factory tritium night sights, an extended, threaded barrel, marine spring cups, modified magazine release, extended slide stop lever (factory standard in newer models), extended +2 magazine baseplates, 15.5 N (3.5 lb<sub>f</sub>) connector, and factory Glock pouch.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-International_74-2"><a href="#cite_note-International-74">[74]</a></sup></li>
<li>The Glock 17DK is a version for <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a>, where handguns must, by law, be at least 210 mm (8.3 in) long. The Glock 17DK has a 122.5 mm (4.8 in) barrel, making the pistol 210 mm (8.3 in) long overall.</li>
<li>The Glock 17 SNF is a version of the Glock 17 used by <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Servicio_Nacional_de_Fronteras_in_Panama&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Servicio Nacional de Fronteras in Panama (page does not exist)">Servicio Nacional de Fronteras in Panama</a> with <i>SNF – Dios y Patria</i> engraved on the slide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-International_74-3"><a href="#cite_note-International-74">[74]</a></sup></li>
<li>The Glock 25 SDN (SDN – <i>Secretaría de la Defensa Nacional</i>) is a version of the Glock 25 for civilian and <a href="/wiki/Law_enforcement_in_Mexico" title="Law enforcement in Mexico">Mexican law enforcement</a> use with <i>S. D. N. MEXICO DF</i> printed in white letters on the right side of the slide. The pistol is chambered for .380 ACP (9mm Kurz, 9mm Short, 9×17mm or 9mm Browning) and is distributed by the Weapon and Ammunition Commercialization Directive (Dirección de Comercialización de Armas y Municiones or DCAM) of SDN<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-International_74-4"><a href="#cite_note-International-74">[74]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Training_variants">Training variants</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glock&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Training variants">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>The Glock 17T training pistol fires paint or rubber bullets. The two versions are easily recognizable from their bright blue frames: the Glock 17T 9 mm FX, which fires <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Simunition&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Simunition (page does not exist)">Simunition FX</a> cartridges and the Glock 17T 7.8×21 AC, which fires cartridges with paint and rubber bullets powered by replaceable pressurized air cartridges.</li>
<li>The Glock 17P, 22P, and Glock 17R are all training pistols for practicing hand-to-hand combat, loading and unloading of the pistol. These Glocks are identical to a standard Glock 17/22 except for their red frame; some models have an inert barrel (without a chamber, thus preventing the accidental chambering of a live cartridge) and no firing pin hole in the breech face (preventing someone from using a live barrel with the training slide). The difference between models is that to perform a 'reset' of the trigger, a cycling of the slide has to be performed on the 17P/22P, but not on the 17R.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Production_in_other_countries">Production in other countries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glock&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Production in other countries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Iraqi_Police_fire_Glock_9mm_handguns.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1632" data-file-width="2464" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Iraqi_Police_fire_Glock_9mm_handguns.jpg/200px-Iraqi_Police_fire_Glock_9mm_handguns.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Iraqi_Police_fire_Glock_9mm_handguns.jpg/300px-Iraqi_Police_fire_Glock_9mm_handguns.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Iraqi_Police_fire_Glock_9mm_handguns.jpg/400px-Iraqi_Police_fire_Glock_9mm_handguns.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Iraqi_Police_fire_Glock_9mm_handguns.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Iraqi police firing 9 mm Glock handguns at a firing range</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Aside from the original Austrian company, Glock pistols are manufactured by the Glock Inc. subsidiary division located in the United States. Those batches are nearly the same or identical compared to the Austrian-made ones, but they are marked as "USA", instead of "AUSTRIA", on the slide; and they have seven-digit serial numbers, instead of the Austrians' six. Glock 17 pistols are being assembled locally at army workshops of <a href="/wiki/Uruguay" title="Uruguay">Uruguay</a> to fulfill the needs of the national military services and law enforcement organizations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FB_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-FB-80">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> These pistols are assembled initially with original Glock parts and later with locally manufactured parts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FB_80-1"><a href="#cite_note-FB-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<p>The 205th Armory in Taiwan produces a copy of the Glock 19, named as the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=T97_pistol&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="T97 pistol (page does not exist)">T97</a>. The Taiwan-made Glocks were made to replace the <a href="/wiki/Smith_%26_Wesson_Model_5906" title="Smith &amp; Wesson Model 5906">Smith &amp; Wesson Model 5906</a> used by the <a href="/wiki/National_Police_Agency_(Republic_of_China)" title="National Police Agency (Republic of China)">Taiwan police</a>, but it ultimately did not enter service. Turkish company <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Akdal_Arms&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Akdal Arms (page does not exist)">Akdal Arms</a> produces a pistol named the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ghost_TR01" title="Ghost TR01">Ghost TR01</a>, which is heavily influenced by Glock pistols in its design.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> Russian firms such as Skat,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/ORSIS" title="ORSIS">ORSIS</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Izhmash" title="Izhmash">Izhmash</a> <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> assembles three models of Glock pistols locally: the Glock 17, 34, and 35. There are three sidearms made by Iranian <a href="/wiki/Defense_Industries_Organization" title="Defense Industries Organization">DIO</a>'s Shahid Kaveh Industry Complex which they call Ra'ad (has a safety selector, possibly an unlicensed copy of Glock 17), Glock 19 and Kaveh-17 (probably an improved Ra'ad, a variant of Glock 17S), which all of them are unlicensed clones of Glock pistols.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> It is not known if they could make their way to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iranian_military" title="Iranian military">Iranian Military</a> and replace the <a href="/wiki/Browning_Hi-Power" title="Browning Hi-Power">Browning Hi-Power</a>, <a href="/wiki/M1911_pistol" title="M1911 pistol">1911</a> and <a href="/wiki/SIG_Sauer_P226" title="SIG Sauer P226">SIG P226</a> pistols and they were possibly some prototypes and have never gone on mass production.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
